<li id="cite_note-russell-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-russell_38-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a href="/wiki/Bertrand_Russell" title="Bertrand Russell">Russell, Bertrand</a> (1927-03-06). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.positiveatheism.org/hist/russell0.htm">"Why I am Not a Christian"</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2006-05-19</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABelief&amp;rft.aufirst=Bertrand&amp;rft.aulast=Russell&amp;rft.btitle=Why+I+am+Not+a+Christian&amp;rft.date=1927-03-06&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.positiveatheism.org%2Fhist%2Frussell0.htm&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example, some <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> believe that women are inferior to men. Some <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christians</a> share this belief. At the time of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, many Southerners used passages from the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> to justify <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>. The Christian religion has been used as a reason to persecute and to deny the rights of homosexuals, on the basis that God disapproves of homosexuality, and by implication homosexuals <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.godhatesfags.com">[2]</a>. Adherents to a religion may feel antipathy to unbelievers.There are countless examples of people of one religion or sect using religion as an excuse to murder people with different religious beliefs. To mention just a few, there was the slaughter of the <a href="/wiki/Huguenot" title="Huguenot">Huguenots</a> by French <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> in the Sixteenth century; <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> killing each other when <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> separated from India in 1947; the persecution and killing of <a href="/wiki/Shiite" class="mw-redirect" title="Shiite">Shiite</a> Muslims by <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> Muslims in Iraq and the murder of <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestants</a> by <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> and vice versa in <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, (both of these examples in the late Twentieth century); and the <a href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a> that continues today. According to some critics of religion, these beliefs can encourage completely unnecessary conflicts and in some cases even wars. Many <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheists</a> believe that, because of this, religion is incompatible with world peace, freedom, civil rights, equality, and good government. On the other hand, most religions perceive atheism as a threat and will vigorously and violently defend themselves against religious sterilization, making the attempt to remove public religious practices a source of strife.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Beauchamp, Philip (pseudonym of Jeremy Bentham) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?hl=en&amp;id=qiRQAAAAIAAJ&amp;dq=Natural+Religion+on+the+Temporal+Happiness+of+Mankind&amp;printsec=frontcover&amp;source=web&amp;ots=sGJSbzT4Ts&amp;sig=pzV-WU5Jx0cpsVXX08ZU17mL-BE&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;resnum=1&amp;ct=result#PPA76,M1">"Analysis of the Influence of Natural Religion on the Temporal Happiness of Mankind"</a>, 1822, R. Carlile, London, at page 76: "Of all human antipathies, that which the believer in a God bears to the unbeliever is the fullest, the most unqualified, and the most universal"</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Faith is the commitment of one‚Äôs consciousness to beliefs for which one has no sensory evidence or rational proof. When a person rejects reason as their standard of judgment, only one alternative standard remains to them: feelings. A mystic is a person who treats feelings as tools of cognition. Faith is the equation of feeling with knowledge. To practice the ‚Äúvirtue‚Ä? of faith, one must be willing to suspend one‚Äôs sight and one‚Äôs judgment; one must be willing to live with the unintelligible, with that which cannot be conceptualized or integrated into the rest of one‚Äôs knowledge, and to induce a trance like illusion of understanding. One must be willing to repress one‚Äôs critical faculty and hold it as one‚Äôs guilt; one must be willing to drown any questions that rise in protest‚Äîto strangle any trust of reason convulsively seeking to assert its proper function as the protector of one‚Äôs life and cognitive integrity. The human need for self-esteem entails the need for a sense of control over reality‚Äîbut no control is possible in a universe which, by one‚Äôs own concession, contains the supernatural, the miraculous and the causeless, a universe in which one is at the mercy of ghosts and demons, in which one must deal, not with the unknown, but with the unknowable; no control is possible if a person proposes, but a ghost disposes; no control is possible if the universe is a haunted house. A person's life and self-esteem require that the object and concern of his or her consciousness be reality and this earth‚Äîbut morality, people are taught, consists of scorning this earth and the world available to sensory perception, and of contemplating, instead, a ‚Äúdifferent‚Ä? and ‚Äúhigher‚Ä? reality, a realm inaccessible to reason and incommunicable in language, but attainable by revelation, by special dialectical processes, by that superior state of intellectual lucidity known to Zen-Buddhists as ‚ÄúNo-Mind,‚Ä? or by death. A person's life and self-esteem require that this person take pride in their power to think, pride in their power to live‚Äîbut morality, people are taught, holds pride, and specifically intellectual pride, as the gravest of sins. Virtue begins, people are taught, with humility: with the recognition of the helplessness, the smallness, the impotence of one‚Äôs mind. A person's life and self-esteem require the person to be loyal to their values, loyal to their mind and its judgments, loyal to their life‚Äîbut the essence of morality, people are taught, consists of self-sacrifice: the sacrifice of one‚Äôs mind to some higher authority, and the sacrifice of one‚Äôs values to whoever may claim to require it. A sacrifice, it is necessary to remember, means the surrender of a higher value in favor of a lower value or of a nonvalue. If one gives up that which one does not value in order to obtain that which one does value‚Äîor if one gives up a lesser value in order to obtain a greater one‚Äîthis is not a sacrifice, but a gain. Remember further that all of a person's values exist in a hierarchy; people value some things more than others; and, to the extent that a person is rational, the hierarchical order of the person's values is rational: that is, the person values things in proportion to their importance in serving this person's life and well-being. That which is inimical to their life and well-being, that which is inimical to their nature and needs as a living being, the person disvalues. Conversely, one of the characteristics of mental illness is a distorted value structure; the neurotic does not value things according to their objective merit, in relation to the person's nature and needs; they frequently value the very things that will lead them to self-destruction. Judged by objective standards, they are engaged in a chronic process of self-sacrifice. But if sacrifice is a virtue, it is not the neurotic but the rational person who must be ‚Äúcured.‚Ä? They must learn to do violence to their own rational judgment‚Äîto reverse the order of their value hierarchy‚Äîto surrender that which their mind has chosen as the good‚Äîto turn against and invalidate their own consciousness.<cite class="citation book">Waldau, Paul (2001). <i>The Specter of Speciesism: Buddhist and Christian Views of Animals (American Academy of Religion Books)</i>. Oxford University Press, USA. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0195145717" title="Special:BookSources/978-0195145717">978-0195145717</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABelief&amp;rft.aufirst=Paul&amp;rft.aulast=Waldau&amp;rft.btitle=The+Specter+of+Speciesism%3A+Buddhist+and+Christian+Views+of+Animals+%28American+Academy+of+Religion+Books%29&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0195145717&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press%2C+USA&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-BitesGlover-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-BitesGlover_42-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BitesGlover_42-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BitesGlover_42-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BitesGlover_42-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BitesGlover_42-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BitesGlover_42-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BitesGlover_42-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BitesGlover_42-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://philosophybites.com/2011/10/jonathan-glover-on-systems-of-belief.html">"Jonathan Glover on systems of belief", Philosophy Bites Podcast, Oct 9 2011</a></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Elizabeth A. Minton, Lynn R. Khale (2014). <i>Belief Systems, Religion, and Behavioral Economics</i>. New York: Business Expert Press LLC. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-60649-704-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-60649-704-3">978-1-60649-704-3</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABelief&amp;rft.au=Elizabeth+A.+Minton%2C+Lynn+R.+Khale&amp;rft.btitle=Belief+Systems%2C+Religion%2C+and+Behavioral+Economics&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-60649-704-3&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=Business+Expert+Press+LLC&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-GloverBeliefs-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-GloverBeliefs_44-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jonathanglover.co.uk/philosophy-beliefs-and-conflicts/philosophy-beliefs-and-conflicts"><i>'Philosophy, Beliefs, and Conflict'</i> , JonathanGlover.co.uk</a></span></li>
